Specification of the coding system for the CLHLS 2008-201 8 longitu dinal dataset (including the 2008, 2011, 2014 , and 201 8 waves of both survivors and deceased persons) Note: please read the following specification BEFORE using this data set. This dataset is derived from the 200 8 , 2011 , 2014, and 2018 waves of the Chinese Longitudinal Healthy Longevity Survey (CLHLS). The CLHLS covers 23 out of 31 provinces in China . This dataset consists of seven components. The first component contains all the information collected in the 200 8 survey for 1 6 ,95 4 respond ents who were interviewed in 2008 . The second component contains information collected in the 2011 survey for 8,4 18 respondents who were re-interviewed in 2011 . The third component includes information collected from the next-of-kin of 5,6 42 deceased persons who were interviewed in 200 8 but had died before the 2011 follow-up survey. The fourth component is the information collected in 2014 for 5,245 respondents who were still alive at the time of the 2014 survey. The fifth component is the information obtained from the next-of-kin of 2 , 589 responde nts who were interviewed in 2008, re-interviewed in 2011 , but died before the 201 4 survey. A very small part of respondents were interviewed for twice in the 2011 wave, one in 2011 and another in 2012 for more in-depth study. Among the 5 ,642 deceased samples, 7 were interviewed in the 2011 survey as survivors during 2008-2011 and died before the 2012 more in-depth survey. The six component contains information collected in the 2018 survey for 2,440 respondents who were interviewed in 2018. The seven component includes information collected from the next-of-kin of 1,547 deceased persons who were interviewed in 2014 but had died before the 2018 follow-up survey. Out of 1 6,954 total respondents who were interviewed in 200 8 , 2,894 respondents we re lost to follow-up in the 2011 survey, d 59 1 respondents were lost to follow-up in the 201 4 survey , and 1,259 respondents were lost to follow-up in the 201 8 survey . This dataset is called the 200 8 -201 8 longitudinal data. It presents both static and ten -year interval dynamic information for the respondents interviewed in 200 8 . 2. Variables and the code system in this data set are based on questions in the individual questionnaire in the 200 8 survey, questions not in shaded boxes in the ind ividual questionnaire in the 2011 , 2014 and 2018 follow-up survey, and questions in the questionnaire for the deceased person in the 2011 , 2014 and 2018 follow-up survey. The names of variables and the code system in this dataset, however, are not necessarily all the same as those in the corresponding questionnaires. Some are slightly different. Please use this coding system when performing analysis, and take the questionnaire as a basic reference. 3. In the cod ing system, ‘Write Format: F3’, for example, means that the length of the code of the variable is 3 digits without decimal points, while ‘Write Format: F8.6’ represents the length of the code of the variable is 8 digits with 6 digits after the decimal point. The latter format (with a decimal point) is used for weights. 4. Most of variables are treated as ‘ Numeric ’ ones in this dataset, while some of them are treated as ‘string’ ones. Variables such as age, year, month, number of persons, and number of days are treated as ‘Scale’ type. Most of the remaining variables are treated as ‘Nominal’ ones including ‘yes’ or ‘no’ binomial questions. Variables in Part B, variables related to ADL, IADL functioning capacity in Part E, and some variables in Part D in the surviving individual questionnaires are treated as ‘Ordinal’ ones. ADL functioning before dying for the deceased persons are also treated as ‘Ordinal’ variables. More detailed information could be found in the ‘measurement level’ in the coding system. 5. A variable with ‘ r ’ as the first letter in the name of the variable is a variable that indicates whether the question was answered personally by the respondent or was answered by a proxy. 6. Variables with names ‘_ 11 ’ , ‘_14’ and ‘_1 8 ’ as their suffix are for those who were still alive and re-interviewed in 2011 , 2014 and 2018 , respectively, while variables with names ‘d 11’ , ‘d14’ and ‘d1 8 ’ as their prefix are variables for those deceased respondents who died in the survey interval of 200 8 -20 11 , 2011 -201 4 and 2014-2018 , respectively. 7 . ‘-6’ is used to indicate that the variable is used for surviving persons ONLY and is NOT applicable to the deceased persons. ‘-7’ is used to indicate that the variable is used for the deceased persons ONLY and is NOT applicable to the surviving respondents, and ‘-9’ is used to define lost to follow-up. ‘–1’ is used in this data set to indicate a situation in which the question is NOT applicable to the respondent. ‘9’, ‘99’, ‘999’, and ‘9999’ are usually used to represent missing information in different variables, while ‘8’, ‘88’, ‘888’, and ‘8888’ in most cases (but NOT all cases) are used to indicate situations in which the respondent didn’t know the answers to the questions. The missing values indicated by ‘8’, ‘88’, ‘888’, ‘8888’, ‘9’, ‘99’, ‘999’, and ‘9999’ need to be imputed by the user before doing the analysis, especially when the proportion of ‘missing’ or ‘don’t know’ is larger than 5%. The data sets with imputed values to replace the missing data are not currently available. 8 . There are four variables (i.e., dth0 8_11, dth11_14 , dth14_18 and w_200 8 ) in this dataset are non-survey variables . The variable of “dth0 8_11” , “dth11_14” and “dth1 4 _1 8 ” indicate survival status in the 2011 , 2014 and 2018 surveys (i.e., surviving, dead, lost to follow-up). Another variable is “w_ 20 08 ” (see Note 1 1 ). 9 . Attention should be given to time-varying variables. The information gathered in the 200 8 survey (e.g., number of marriages, information about the last marriage) is subject to change. 1 0 . Geographic codes indicating participants ’ county/city/town residence location in 1998, 2000, 2002, 2005 , 2008, 2011, 2014, and 2018 waves are NOT included in this released dataset. This is because that some counties have very small number of participants; consequently, releasing participants ’ county/city/town residence loca tion codes would violate the rules for protecting individuals ’ private confidentiality. 1 1 . The weight variable “w_2008” is estimated based on the numbers of elderly persons by age, sex, and rural/urban residence in 2008 from the 2010 census 100% data tabulations for the 23 provinces where the 2008 survey was conducted. The total number of the weighted individual cases of the survey is equal to the total sample size. However, the numbers of the weighted individual cases for the age-sex-residence-specific groups may not be exactly the same as the actual sub-sample size of the corresponding groups. Thus, SPSS, SAS, STATA (or other software) would not produce correct p-values for testing the statistical significance of the differences of the average proportions across different age-sex-reference groups, since the sub-sample size of the sub-groups may be altered after weighting the individual cases. Therefore, the weights need to be appropriately adjusted to ensure that the sub-sample size within each sub-group after weighting is exactly the same as the true sub-sample size for the cross sub-groups comparisons by using statistical significance tests. Such adjusted weights are available upon request. Please refer to Zeng and Vaupel et al. (2001: Appendix A) for details on how the weights and the adjusted weights are computed. Weight is not applied to those respondents aged less than 65 or more than 106 at their first interviews. 1 2 . The eligible respondents in this data set are those people aged 65 and over. There are a very few respondents in this data set whose age was less than 65 at the baseline survey, however. It’s recommended to exclude the respondents who were less than 65 years. 1 3 . This dataset can be available in SPSS, SAS, STATA, or ASCII format. Please indicate which format you prefer. 1 4 . This codebook is produced by S TATA 1 4 .1. 1 5 . This is the released Version 1.0 for the 200 8 -201 8 longitudinal dataset. It is highly appreciated that you contact us with your comments or found errors, which is important for the improvement of this dataset in the future.
